section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">G</span>ood evening. Here is a round up of today\'s main coronavirus developments:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Nicola Sturgeon <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2020/10/07/wednesday-evening-news-briefing-pubs-ordered-shut/">imposed\xc2\xa0new restrictions on pubs and cafes across Scotland</a> - including a complete ban on indoor alcohol sales in pubs, with hospitality settings now takeaway-only throughout 60 per cent of the country.</li>\n<li>The First Minister insisted that it is not another coronavirus lockdown, but <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/politics/2020/10/07/sturgeon-shuts-pubs-restaurants-across-central-belt-hands-death/">was accused of handing a \'death sentence\' to hospitality businesses</a>, with amateur sports and entertainment venues also hits.</li>\n<li>South of the border Matt Hancock, the Health Secretary,<a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2020/10/07/health-secretary-hints-pubs-could-forced-shut-no-10-mulls-traffic/"> hinted that pubs could also be forced to shut here if a \'traffic-light system\'\xc2\xa0for local lockdowns</a> - on which no final decision has yet been made - were to be introduced.</li>\n<li>A further 14,162 laboratory-confirmed cases of Covid-19 have been announced by the Department for Health, taking the UK\'s overall caseload to 544,275. A further 70 deaths were also confirmed across all settings.</li>\n<li>Newcastle and Northumbria universities have <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2020/10/07/universities-accused-misleading-students-pretending-would-have/">become the latest to move all teaching online</a> amid accusations that students were \xe2\x80\x9clured\xe2\x80\x9d into believing they would be able to enjoy a \xe2\x80\x9cfull campus experience\xe2\x80\x9d.</li>\n<li><a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2020/10/07/brussels-closes-cafes-belgium-announces-rule-four-combat-coronavirus/">Brussels\' cafes and bars will close for a month</a>, it was announced on Wednesday after Belgium said it would introduce a nationwide &quot;rule of four&quot; to\xc2\xa0curb rising coronavirus infections.</li>\n<li>The world is <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/global-health/science-and-disease/lives-put-risk-pipeline-coronavirus-antivirals-bare-experts/">at risk of a \xe2\x80\x9creal deficit\xe2\x80\x9d of high quality coronavirus treatments, putting millions of lives at risk</a>, as the pipeline for new antiviral drugs is \xe2\x80\x9cbare\xe2\x80\x9d, experts have warned.</li>\n<li><a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/business/2020/10/07/greene-king-cuts-800-jobs-curfew-rule-hits-pubs/">Greene King is to cut up to 800 jobs and shut dozens of pubs</a> after warning that\xc2\xa0ministers\'\xc2\xa010pm curfew\xc2\xa0has trashed the hospitality industry.\xc2\xa0</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong><a warns</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he OBR has warned that ballooning government debt\xc2\xa0means the UK was increasingly exposed to the risk of interest rates rising in the coming years and decades, writes\xc2\xa0<strong>Tim Wallace</strong>.</p>\n<p>Richard Hughes told MPs that the Government should not rely on\xc2\xa0borrowing costs staying at record lows\xc2\xa0forever when drawing up tax and spending plans.</p>\n<p>\xe2\x80\x9cWe are clearly in exceptional times at the moment, with very low interest rates,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mr Hughes.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="articleBodyImage \xe2\x80\x9cwill come as a crushing blow\xe2\x80\x9d to hospitality.</p>\n<p>While claiming control of the virus is central to permanent economic recovery, she said that\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x9chospitality, leisure and tourism firms will rightly be frustrated at this decision, having invested heavily in making their premises as safe as possible for employees and because pipeline for coronavirus antivirals is &#39;bare&#39;, warn experts</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">W</span>hile potentially far-off coronavirus vaccines have received around $2 billion of investment, <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2020/09/02/5-drug-cuts-risk-dying-coronavirus-fifth-rolled-across-nhs/">funding for treatments</a> currently totals just $300 million.</p>\n<p>The world is at risk of a \xe2\x80\x9creal deficit\xe2\x80\x9d of high quality coronavirus treatments, putting millions of lives at risk, as the pipeline for new antiviral drugs is \xe2\x80\x9cbare\xe2\x80\x9d, experts have warned.</p>\n<p>Speaking at a virtual briefing Dr Nick Cammack, who is leading the global search for Covid therapeutics at Wellcome, said there is not enough focus on developing new treatments designed specifically to tackle coronaviruses.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="articleBodyImage section">\n<div class="article-body-image component " itemscope They closed all cafes and bars in the city for a month from 7am on Thursday. Drinking in public places is banned, but restaurants can remain open.\xc2\xa0\n<br/>\n<br/> Nationwide restrictions announced on Tuesday ordered bars and cafes to\xc2\xa0close early at time</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he Czech Republic has reported a record 4,457 new coronavirus cases in the space of a single day, with infections now rising at Europe\xe2\x80\x99s fastest pace according to the Reuters news agency.</p>\n<p>The Czech Republic\'s 14-day case rate is\xc2\xa0now at 326.8 cases per 100,000, with tightened measures set to be announced as of Friday.</p>\n<p><span style="">There is currently no travel corridor between the Czech Republic and the UK, and it is unlikely one will be formed anytime soon.</span></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post pubs and restaurants across central belt in &#39;death sentence&#39; to businesses</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">A</span>ll pubs, bars and restaurants serving more than half of Scotland\'s population are to shut for at least 16 days from this weekend, under complicated rules unveiled by Nicola Sturgeon to prevent Covid-19 surging back to its spring peak, reports <strong>Simon Johnson</strong>.</p>\n<p>The First Minister announced all licensed premises in the Central Belt, except hotels for residents and takeaways, must close indoors and outdoors from 6pm on Friday. The tough measures will apply in five health board areas covering around 3.3 million people.</p>\n<p>In the remainder of the country, licensed premises can open for indoors service between 6am and 6pm but will be barred from selling alcoholic drinks.\xc2\xa0Ms Sturgeon also requested shops across Scotland return to two-metre distancing and one-way systems.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div Indoor environments inevitably produce a greater risk of transmission. And of course the presence of alcohol can affect people\'s willingness to physically distance.&quot;</p>\n<p><span class="m_first-letter">M</span>s Sturgeon says restrictions on hospitality for 16 days will significantly restrict the spread of the virus across that timescale.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost60" data-timestamp="54545">\n<div class="component-content live-post__wrapper">\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body">\n<a href="#update-20201007-1509"><time class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" datetime="2020-10-07T15:09:29.833+01:00">3:09PM</time></a>\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body-article">\n<h3 class="live-post__title">Scotland lockdown restrictions: &#39;Central Belt&#39; i.e. going to school or work.</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost59" data-timestamp="52758">\n<div class="component-content live-post__wrapper">\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body">\n<a href="#update-20201007-1505"><time class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" datetime="2020-10-07T15:05:47.087+01:00">3:05PM</time></a>\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body-article">\n<h3 class="live-post__title">New Scotland lockdown rules set out by Nicola Sturgeon</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he First Minister describes the ban on indoor household mixing as &quot;the most important measure&quot; she says. &quot;I am acutely aware that this is and cannot be a one-dimensional decision. We have a duty to balance all of the different harms caused by the pandemic.&quot;</p>\n<p>The following measures are set out over the course of 16 days with the exceptions of five health board areas which will see stricter limits still:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Pubs, restaurants, bars and cafes will be able to operate indoors between 6am and 6pm for the service of food and non-alcoholic drinks</li>\n<li>Hotel restaurants will be able to operate after 6pm for residents only and without alcohol</li>\n<li>Pubs, restaurants, bars and cafes can continue to serve alcohol outdoors up to 10pm</li>\n<li>There will be an exemption on the alcohol ban for weddings that are already booked and for funerals</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost58" data-timestamp="52379">\n<div class="component-content live-post__wrapper">\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body">\n<a href="#update-20201007-1459"><time class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" datetime="2020-10-07T14:59:27.554+01:00">2:59PM</time></a>\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body-article">\n<h3 class="live-post__title">Nicola Sturgeon: &#39;Without action, we are likely to return to peak levels&#39;</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">M</span>s Sturgeon describes the measures that are to be announced as &quot;tough but necessary&quot;. are rising across the country&quot;, with Orkney and Shetland the only exceptions to this.</p>\n<p>&quot;Without action, and this is the starkest warning in today\'s evidence paper, we are likely to sector, MPs told</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he UK is not doing enough to eradicate sexual abuse and exploitation within the aid and humanitarian sector, experts told MPs on Tuesday.\xc2\xa0</p>\n<p>There have long been concerns about sexual abuse and exploitation perpetrated by United Nations peacekeepers. And charities have also come under scrutiny after it emerged in 2018\xc2\xa0that Oxfam staff had paid young women in Haiti for sex while responding to the 2010 earthquake.</p>\n<p>While many governments and humanitarian organisations have since promised a \xe2\x80\x9czero tolerance\xe2\x80\x9d of abuse, there is little evidence this has had any impact, said Paula Donovan co-director of the Code Blue Campaign to end impunity for sexual exploitation and abuse by UN peacekeepers.</p>\n<p>Just last week an investigation by the Thomson Reuters Foundation and The New Humanitarian revealed<a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/global-health/women-and-girls/international-aid-workers-accused-sexual-abuse-congos-two-year/">\xc2\xa051 women had accused mainly foreign aid workers of forcing them into sex</a>\xc2\xa0during an Ebola outbreak in the DRC between 2018-2020.</p>\n<p>Abuse and exploitation is endemic within the aid sector and the UK has the power to stop this happening and hold agents to account, Ms Donoavan told the International Development Committee.</p>\n<p><strong>Jordan Kelly-Linden <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/global-health/climate-and-people/uk-not-enough-end-impunity-sexual-exploitation-aid-sector-mps/">has the story</a></strong>.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost44" data-timestamp="45742">\n<div class="component-content height of the pandemic.</p>\n<p>Talking to The Telegraph\'s <strong>Henry Bodkin</strong>, Peter Walsh,\xc2\xa0from\xc2\xa0patient safety charity Action against Medical Accidents, said:</p>\n<blockquote>\nIt is not the case of this just being about people having been reluctant to make use of the NHS. Many people have been trying to and not been allowed to.\n<br/>\n<br/> There has already been avoidable death and harm as a consequence, yet there appears to be no acknowledgement of that.\n<br/>\n<br/> Whilst I appreciate Ms Pritchard\xe2\x80\x99s ambition to remain open to all during the pandemic and encouragement of those with doubts to seek help from the NHS, there needs to be more realism.\n<br/>\n<br/> There is a huge backlog to catch up with and evidence suggests that there are likely to be many avoidable deaths and harm \xc2\xa0as a result of the disruption. travel</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he world\'s first coronavirus\xc2\xa0passport is being launched today to enable people to travel without\xc2\xa0having to quarantine, writes our home affairs editor\xc2\xa0<strong>Charles Hymas</strong>.</p>\n<p>Passengers using two of the world\'s biggest airlines \xe2\x80\x93 United Airlines and Cathay Pacific \xe2\x80\x93 and travelling through London Heathrow will be the first to test\xc2\xa0the technology, which is backed by the US government.</p>\n<p>The volunteer passengers will upload their coronavirus test results from a validated laboratory onto a digital health passport up to 72 hours before departure. The airlines, and airport and border officials, will be able to scan the digital data on the pass to see if a person is free of the virus.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="articleBodyImage infections.</p>\n<p>Under the new rules, restaurants, pubs and shops will be forced to close between 11pm and 6am.</p>\n<p>Pharmacies and petrol stations will be exempt but will not be allowed to sell outdoors by day, while indoor gatherings will be limited to 10 day and night.</p>\n<p>Berlin currently has one of the highest weekly infection rates in Germany, with 40.5 new cases per 100,000 Homeless have to choose between rough sleeping and catching Covid in shelters</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">I</span>n a letter to Communities Secretary Robert Jenrick, Sadiq Khan called on the Government to provide funding and guidance for those working with homeless people to protect them from cold temperatures and Covid-19.</p>\n<p>In a typical year, winter night shelters start to open in November as temperatures fall, often providing communal sleeping spaces in church halls or community buildings.</p>\n<p>These night shelters - run by charities, voluntary organisations and faith groups - hosted around 700 people in the capital last year.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="articleBodyImage section">\n<div class="article-body-image component " itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" funding for Covid-safe alternatives.</p>\n<p>Recent figures show more than 900 people are sleeping rough on the streets of the capital.</p>\n<p>Mr Khan called for the Government to fully fund safe experts warn</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he Royal College of Psychiatrists said waiting times for mental health services could &quot;get a lot worse&quot;.</p>\n<p>The college said its poll of 513 British adults with a mental illness found that many patients face lengthy waits between their initial assessment and next appointment - with some patients ending up in A&amp;E.</p>\n<p>Almost two fifths (38%) reported that they or someone on their behalf had contacted emergency or crisis services while waiting for their second appointment, while 39% said waiting led to a decline in their mental health, the college said.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, the figures revealed that one in 10 of those polled (11%) waited longer than six months between their initial assessment and second appointment.</p>\n<p>Almost a quarter (23%) waited more than three months and 64% waited more than a month.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" datetime="2020-10-07T07:14:54.843+01:00">7:14AM</time></a>\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body-article">\n<h3 class="live-post__title">Chicken factor installs disinfectant booths</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">A</span> chicken factory where more than 130 workers tested positive for coronavirus has installed disinfectant spraying booths at its entrances.</p>\n<p>Banham Poultry in Attleborough, Norfolk, was forced to partially close for around two weeks from late August.</p>\n<p>It has since re-opened with additional safety measures, including five disinfectant machines at entrances to its factories and offices.</p>\n<p>The walk-in booths are equipped with artificial intelligence and facial recognition technology to identify employees and check their body temperatures.</p>\n<p>Users walk through the booth and their outer layers are covered in a fine mist of vaporised disinfectant before they enter the building.</p>\n<p>The site also uses portable hand-held machines that spray a fine mist of disinfectant.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost14" data-timestamp="23608">\n<div class="component-content live-post__wrapper">\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body">\n<a href="#update-20201007-0659"><time class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" chain of transmission</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he clinical trial, led by scientists at University College London (UCL), will evaluate the use of real-time viral genomic data to reduce the spread of Covid-19 within hospitals.</p>\n<p>The findings could help the NHS reduce further transmission by determining if an individual caught the virus from someone else within the same hospital, researchers say.</p>\n<p>Professor Judith Breuer, the trial lead, said: &quot;Spread of Covid-19 infections in hospitals is now recognised to be a major problem for both healthcare workers and patients, and breaking the chain of these transmissions is critical.</p>\n<p><span style="">&quot;It is essential that we try out new tools such as viral sequencing to find out why this is happening and to help reduce hospital spread.&quot;</span></p>\n<p>The study, together with the UCL comprehensive clinical trials unit (CCTU), forms part of the Government\'s \xc2\xa320 million Covid-19 Genomics UK Consortium (Cog-UK) which allows scientists to map the virus\' spread across the country.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" datetime="2020-10-07T06:42:05.108+01:00">6:42AM</time></a>\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body-article">\n<h3 class="live-post__title">Fifth of parents increased financial support for children during pandemic</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">S</span>ome 21% of parents in this age group with children aged over 18 said they have been offering them more financial support than usual since March, a survey has found.</p>\n<p>The research, from the Saga Equity Release Advice Service, found that some parents have dipped into their savings to do this, or have cut back on spending on themselves.</p>\n<p>Others have given money that they would otherwise have left as part of their inheritance.</p>\n<p>Common reasons over-50s parents have increased their financial support include their children having been furloughed, losing their job, or suffering debt problems.</p>\n<p>Some parents also wanted to help their children buy a home in light of the temporary stamp duty holiday.</p>\n<p>Alex Edmans, head of equity release said what is right for one family may not be appropriate for everyone, adding: &quot;Decisions should be made based on individual needs and circumstances.&quot;</p>\n<p>More than 1,400 parents aged over 50 with adult children were surveyed.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost12" data-timestamp="21680">\n<div class="component-content live-post__wrapper">\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body">\n<a href="#update-20201007-0627"><time class="live-post__wrapper-body-timestamp-full" datetime="2020-10-07T06:27:49.331+01:00">6:27AM</time></a>\n<div class="live-post__wrapper-body-article">\n<h3 class="live-post__title">Hospital criticised for failing to comply with Covid rules</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>he William Harvey Hospital, run by East Kent Hospitals University NHS Foundation Trust, was inspected by the Care Quality Commission (CQC) on August 11.</p>\n<p>The inspectors ordered &quot;urgent enforcement action&quot; by requiring that the emergency department was risk-assessed for social distancing and coronavirus risks.</p>\n<p>They found that staff did not always wear personal protective equipment (PPE) correctly in medical wards as well as on the Covid-19 ward, with a member of the nursing team also seen incorrectly wearing a mask on a ward which had seen an outbreak of the disease.</p>\n<p>They also found that staff did not always use alcohol hand gel on entering and leaving wards and at least seven members of staff were seen entering and leaving a ward caring for patients with suspected Covid-19 without washing their hands properly.</p>\n<p>The emergency department staff also did not always have access to hand gel or hand washing facilities, with hand sanitiser dispensers remaining empty at both entrances even after the inspectors had raised the issue.</p>\n<p>And inspectors found there was an inconsistent approach to triaging patients with Covid-19 symptoms in the emergency department.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">S</span>outh Korea has reported 114 new cases of coronavirus, its first daily jump of more than 100 in a week.</p>\n<p>Health officials had raised concerns that infections would rise because of increased travel during the Chuseok harvest holiday that ended on Sunday.</p>\n<p>Ninety-two of the cases reported on Wednesday by the Korea Disease Control and Prevention Agency were from the Seoul metropolitan area, where the virus has been resurgent since mid-August.</p>\n<p>Health officials have been struggling to track transmissions linked to various places, including an army unit in Pocheon, where 37 troops have tested class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">T</span>here has been Association, said: &quot;If the Scottish Government is to implement further harsh restrictive measures to our sector, it must include a dedicated package of support alongside it.</p>\n<p>&quot;Without button.&quot;</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost7" data-timestamp="19862">\n<div class="component-content class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">N</span>icola Sturgeon is due to announce new\xc2\xa0coronavirus\xc2\xa0restrictions in a statement to the Scottish Parliament on Wednesday afternoon.</p>\n<p>The First Minister is expected to set out the details of the next steps the Scottish Government will take at around 2.50pm.</p>\n<p>She has said the new measures will not amount to Scotland going into another lockdown as was the case in March.</p>\n<p>The announcement will follow a cabinet meeting on Wednesday morning when details of the new restrictions will be decided.</p>\n<p>The First Minister has described the situation as &quot;the most difficult decision point we have faced so far&quot;.</p>\n<p>However, the closure of schools has been ruled out, as have Scotland-wide travel restrictions.</p>\n<p>There will be no requirement for people to stay inside their homes most of the time, as was the case in March, though some additional measures in &quot;hotspot&quot; areas might be necessary.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="live-post  js-live-post component" id="livepost6" data-timestamp="19392">\n<div class="component-content class="live-post__title">&#39;If he still has Covid, we shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have a debate&#39;</h3>\n<div class="articleBodyText section">\n<div class="article-body-text component  ">\n<div class="component-content">\n<p><span class="m_first-letter m_first-letter--flagged">D</span>emocratic presidential candidate Joe Biden said on Tuesday that next week\'s scheduled debate with Republican President Donald Trump should not take place if Mr Trump is still infected with Covid-19.</p>\n<p>Mr Biden said the October 15 debate in Miami should only be staged under strict health guidelines and called the\xc2\xa0coronavirus\xc2\xa0outbreak that has hit Mr Trump and a wave of other White House officials &quot;a very serious problem&quot;.</p>\n<p>&quot;If he still has Covid, we His doctor said on Tuesday that Mr Trump reported no Covid symptoms and was doing &quot;extremely well&quot;.</p>\n<p>The normal quarantine period for anyone testing positive for coronavirus\xc2\xa0is
